  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_1a6ecb53-d36b-4a68-a672-66612dd41227'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

  <span id="freeText672447827861095103" style="display:none">Five months ago, Valerie Leftman's boyfriend, Nick, opened fire on their school cafeteria. Shot trying to stop him, Valerie inadvertently saved the life of a classmate, but was implicated in the shootings because of the list she helped create. A list of people and things she and Nick hated. The list he used to pick his targets.<br /><br />Now, after a summer of seclusion, Val is forced to confront her guilt as she returns to school to complete her senior year. Haunted by the memory of the boyfriend she still loves and navigating rocky relationships with her family, former friends and the girl whose life she saved, Val must come to grips with the tragedy that took place and her role in it, in order to make amends and move on with her life.<br /></span>

<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/1167668-would-you-recommend-this-book-for-someone">Would you recommend this book for someone who likes 13 Reasons Why?</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_1167668'><a id="like_count_community_question_1167668" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/1167668?resource_type=CommunityQuestion"><span class="likesCount">7 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F6316171-hate-list">like</a></span>

</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionTimestamp'>
<a href="/questions/1167668-would-you-recommend-this-book-for-someone">3 years ago</a>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/50938238-shannon-fay"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1451740716i/50938238._UX100_CR0,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/50938238-shannon-fay">Shannon Fay</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">I would absolutely recommend this book to anyone who enjoyed 13 Reason Why. A lot of what it deals with is similar. There's a tragic act that seriousl<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I would absolutely recommend this book to anyone who enjoyed 13 Reason Why. A lot of what it deals with is similar. There's a tragic act that seriously affects people who knew that person. There are people left devastated by those actions, and the main character really struggles, and you can relate to her story, and (at least I could), feel what she's feeling. So if you liked 13 Reasons, because you liked reading about a messed up situation, and how that affects people (I guess liked is the wrong word, cuz it is really messed up). If you enjoyed reading a really tough, but touching book, then yes, you'd probably like this.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

<div id="review_1431116437" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1431116437" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1431116437?book_show_action=true">Nov 01, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780316041454" href="/book/show/7893725-hate-list">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2015">2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1431116437" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14682826206182640290"><blockquote>
  <i>“People do it all the time--assume that they "know" what's going on in someone else's head. That's impossible. And to think it's possible is a mistake. A really big mistake. A life-ruining one if you're not careful.” </i>
</blockquote><br/>This is the kind of story I was hoping for when I read <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/24529123.This_Is_Where_It_Ends' title='This Is Where It Ends by Marieke Nijkamp' rel='nofollow noopener'>This Is Where It Ends</a> - a book that promised to delve into the darkness of school shootings, but never moved past a surface view of mindlessly evil shooter vs. poor victims. <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7893725.Hate_List' title='Hate List by Jennifer Brown' rel='nofollow noopener'>Hate List</a>, on the other hand, is <b>dark, psychologic</b></span>
  <span id="freeText14682826206182640290" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>“People do it all the time--assume that they "know" what's going on in someone else's head. That's impossible. And to think it's possible is a mistake. A really big mistake. A life-ruining one if you're not careful.” </i>
</blockquote><br />This is the kind of story I was hoping for when I read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/24529123.This_Is_Where_It_Ends" title="This Is Where It Ends by Marieke Nijkamp" rel="nofollow noopener">This Is Where It Ends</a> - a book that promised to delve into the darkness of school shootings, but never moved past a surface view of mindlessly evil shooter vs. poor victims. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7893725.Hate_List" title="Hate List by Jennifer Brown" rel="nofollow noopener">Hate List</a>, on the other hand, is <b>dark, psychological, sad and angering</b>.<br /><br />So many things were running through my head while reading this upsetting novel. One was an Abigail Haas quote: <i>"Wouldn't we all look guilty, if someone searched hard enough?"</i> And another was a memory of something I wrote in my diary when I was about thirteen. Back when I was an angsty, depressed teenager, I wrote the sentence: "some people should really just die."<br /><br />That came back to me while reading this book. I was angry, I was sad, but did I want to kill anyone? No. Did I have it in me to get a gun and shoot my classmates? It would never even have occurred to me. And that's kind of what this book is about. How we all have dark thoughts now and then. How we all throw away casual sentences like "I could kill her!" but mean nothing by it.<br /><br />The story, while technically about a school shooting, actually goes far deeper than that. The author chooses to focus not quite on the shooter, not quite on the victims, but on someone in between. Valerie. She was Nick's girlfriend and helped create the "Hate List" - a list of people who had bullied them, humiliated them, judged them. But it was just a harmless list of names, right?<br /><br />Well, it was until Nick decided to walk into school one morning and pick off the people on that list, one by one, and then kill himself. Now, Valerie's left alive with the blame. Many believe she and Nick planned the shooting, many blame her for creating the list regardless. Her own parents can't look at her. Her group of friends are afraid to be associated with her.<br /><br /><b>Valerie is a very sympathetic character</b>. It's easy to relate to her, to feel her pain, her guilt, her loneliness and her anger. Everybody hates sometimes, and it is extremely heartbreaking to see her private hatred dragged out for the world to see and to judge. It made me so angry that she was being blamed for writing down the names of those who made her life hell.<br /><br />And, through her, Nick is not merely an evil boy with a gun. He becomes a human being full of pain and sadness, sick of being kicked into the dirt and treated like shit just for being different. This book breaks down the barriers between victim and villain, between the average teenager and one capable of doing something so horrific.<br /><br />Whenever school shootings happen, people always look for an answer to those same questions: what makes this kid different from everyone else? Do they have some innate propensity to kill? How am I different? Oh god, am I that different? And I think this book really looks at that, humanizing everyone and offering an understanding of their individual situations and motivations.<br /><br />It was very powerful and never once stopped making me feel something - sad, angry, frustrated, concerned, and hopeful.<br /><br /><a href="http://thebookgeek.org" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/EmilyMayTheBookGeek" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="https://www.pinterest.com/bookgeekreviews/" rel="nofollow noopener">Pinterest</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="14682826206182640290" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2408281963" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2408281963" />
    <a title="Lala BooksandLala" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31027440-lala-booksandlala"><img alt="Lala BooksandLala" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597009469p2/31027440.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2408281963?book_show_action=true">Apr 30, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lala BooksandLala" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lala BooksandLala" href="/user/show/31027440-lala-booksandlala">Lala BooksandLala</a>

        rated it

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2408281963" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7924622449081224660">Wow, this book was smart. It really delved into the aftermath of trauma from so many angles, ones that make you mad as a reader, and ones that make you hopeful. The writing itself changed and matured throughout the book, which was a bit jarring, but the subject matter is important and handled well in my opinion.</span>

<div id="review_160837578" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/160837578" />
    <a title="Stacia (the 2010 club)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club"><img alt="Stacia (the 2010 club)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1417661051p2/4013351.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/160837578?book_show_action=true">Apr 13, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stacia (the 2010 club)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stacia (the 2010 club)" href="/user/show/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club">Stacia (the 2010 club)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780316041454" href="/book/show/7893725-hate-list">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=realistic-general-or-lit-fiction">realistic-general-or-lit-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=dark-or-taboo">dark-or-taboo</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer160837578" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16020251774579049326"><b>3.5 stars</b>. After sitting on my thoughts for a day, I feel like I can't review this book with any sort of polished thought process, so I'm just going to let my fingers type out whatever comes to mind. I think this book probably deserves a 4 star plus rating because it is a story worth telling and a story worth reading, but a few things held me back from going higher.<br/><br/>1. <i>The timing was off for me.</i> Given that my state has been rocked by several shootings over the past several years (the most recent </span>
  <span id="freeText16020251774579049326" style="display:none"><b>3.5 stars</b>. After sitting on my thoughts for a day, I feel like I can't review this book with any sort of polished thought process, so I'm just going to let my fingers type out whatever comes to mind. I think this book probably deserves a 4 star plus rating because it is a story worth telling and a story worth reading, but a few things held me back from going higher.<br /><br />1. <i>The timing was off for me.</i> Given that my state has been rocked by several shootings over the past several years (the most recent being the movie theater one; the most upsetting for me personally being the one that happened in my town not long ago at a church we've participated in activities at), I think my mind was having a hard time processing the fact that I was reading this book as <i>fiction</i>, for the sake of entertainment. I might have been better off picking up a real account, such as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/5632446.Columbine" title="Columbine by Dave Cullen" rel="nofollow noopener">Columbine</a> instead. I'm not saying that <i>Hate List</i> trivialized the severity of the subject for the purpose of cheap thrills. I've used the word "entertainment" very lightly in this regard. The subject matter was absolutely handled with the utmost of respect.<br /><br />2. <i>Books like this should be required reading for kids around the middle school age range.</i> Kids <i>need</i> to be told over and over just how bad bullying is. This book managed to show many perspectives on a school shooting, but the one perspective that stood out to me the most was how one person felt like if they'd been a little kinder, there might have been a chance that the entire chain reaction of events might not have been triggered. ONE person out of the many bullies tormenting the offender might have been able to prevent something so horrendous from happening.<br /><br />3. <i>Most of the book felt cold to me.</i> I can't explain why I felt detached, but I was. It wasn't until the very last section that everything hit me in a big way (it appears that a few other friends thought the same thing), and then I started to cry. The book was worth reading just for the way I felt about the last section, but there was something about the setup which felt sterile to me. Maybe that was the point, who knows...but some of the past and present transitions could have been handled a little smoother. <br /><br />4. <i>I appreciated that both of the parties (directly and indirectly) involved with the shootings were shown as feeling, thinking, human beings.</i> Too often, we fail to look at the person committing the crime and wonder how they got to such a place that would make them want to hurt other people. This passage near the end of the book made me lose it (I'm not going to consider it a spoiler that you'll figure out the shooter killed himself because that happens a good portion of the time with these types of crimes, so it's something the majority of us would probably assume to be something that would happen) :<br /><br /><b>Of course Ma would have wanted Nick remembered as a "Beloved Son." Of course she'd do it in the most laid-back way possible - whispering it to him in tiny letters on his headstone. Just a whisper. <i>You were beloved, son. You were my beloved. Even after all of this, I still remember the beloved you. I can't forget.</i></b><br /><br />Even the worst person on earth might still have someone there, remembering them after they are gone - remembering not only the bad, but also the good, the part of that person worth loving.<br /><br />Just typing that out had me fighting back tears. Maybe if Nick had realized just how loved he was, he wouldn't have felt the need to kill those on the "hate list," those people who bullied him. I guess we'll never know. </span>
  <a data-text-id="16020251774579049326" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2431391100" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2431391100" />
    <a title="Tani" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/63414753-tani"><img alt="Tani" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521292450p2/63414753.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2431391100?book_show_action=true">Jun 27, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tani" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tani" href="/user/show/63414753-tani">Tani</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/25185474-hate-list">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">YA fans who don't want romance in a book</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/63414753-tani?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2431391100" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10284269173716531415"><b> RATINGS: 4 STARS</b> <br/><br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7893725.Hate_List' title='Hate List by Jennifer Brown' rel='nofollow noopener'>Hate List</a> is one of the intriguing, catchy and compelling books which makes you think deeply about every side of a crime. A criminal is rejected and punished by the society to justify the victims. The question arises when a criminal is a victim of the society. This book deals with the aftermath of a school shooting. Whenever we watch a news channel, we don't realise how deeply any incident affects the people related to it. This book shows us different sides of a crime, a crimin</span>
  <span id="freeText10284269173716531415" style="display:none"><b> RATINGS: 4 STARS</b> <br /><br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7893725.Hate_List" title="Hate List by Jennifer Brown" rel="nofollow noopener">Hate List</a> is one of the intriguing, catchy and compelling books which makes you think deeply about every side of a crime. A criminal is rejected and punished by the society to justify the victims. The question arises when a criminal is a victim of the society. This book deals with the aftermath of a school shooting. Whenever we watch a news channel, we don't realise how deeply any incident affects the people related to it. This book shows us different sides of a crime, a criminal and the society to emphasise that not everything can be categorised as good or bad. <br /><br /><br />Valerie returns back to her school after her boyfriend, Nick, opened fire on the school cafeteria resulting the deaths and the injuries of the students. She is implicated to the killing as she was involved with Nick to create the Hate List which Nick used to pick his targets. Even though she saved the life of her fellow classmate, she is blamed by everyone including her own family for being part of the shooting. The best thing is that the book neither superficial nor depressing. It deals with the hardest stuff without making it overwhelming, preachy and judgemental. Valerie is a pessimistic, complex and a tad whiny character but considering what she went through, I think anyone who'd be in her shoes would've done the same. The author has done a great job in writing Valerie’s point of view. Her transformation is complex which gives an unfeigned edge to the book. We can't agree with Nick's actions but at the same time, we feel sad for him because of his vulnerability. The author tried her best to show that everyone isn't the stereotypical characters as we assume them to be.<br /><br /><br />I couldn't connect to the book as much I wanted to. The unsupportive nature of Valerie’s parents and at the end, of her brother irked me. Jeremy wasn't included in the rest of the book even though he was one of the characters who influenced Nick negatively. Overall, it's one of the powerful book with a beautiful story.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10284269173716531415" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Faye, la Patata" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Faye, la Patata" href="/user/show/7650833-faye-la-patata">Faye, la Patata</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer652690620" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer15690966042889949122">What a disappointing book. GAH. I'm so mad.<br/><br/>Whiny heroine, whiny parents, whiny brother, whiny friends. I just can't stand it. And why is she trying to force the idea that Nick was still a good guy even if he shot and killed several people? Don't fucking make excuses for him. Ugh. <br/><br/>I mean seriously, the dad threatened to disown the girl! The mom told her outright that <i>she</i> ruined her life for simply loving the wrong guy. She wasn't even the criminal and yet her family treats her like one. What kind</span>
  <span id="freeText15690966042889949122" style="display:none">What a disappointing book. GAH. I'm so mad.<br /><br />Whiny heroine, whiny parents, whiny brother, whiny friends. I just can't stand it. And why is she trying to force the idea that Nick was still a good guy even if he shot and killed several people? Don't fucking make excuses for him. Ugh. <br /><br />I mean seriously, the dad threatened to disown the girl! The mom told her outright that <i>she</i> ruined her life for simply loving the wrong guy. She wasn't even the criminal and yet her family treats her like one. What kind of parents are these? And the heroine didn't report them to the police or to a social worker or something, to how they are treating her? If my parents acted like this, I'd be running away. Nobody deserves that kind of crap, especially from people who should automatically be by your side through thick and thin. I couldn't believe how extreme they were written. Not cool. I was very uncomfortable.<br /><br />Aside from that, the constant wallowing in self-pity was too exhausting. Not recommending this.</span>

<div id="review_69099615" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/69099615" />
    <a title="Kristi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1310688-kristi"><img alt="Kristi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1496094866p2/1310688.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/69099615?book_show_action=true">Aug 27, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kristi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kristi" href="/user/show/1310688-kristi">Kristi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer69099615" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6773302836807723993">Three words: Powerful, thought-provoking, & riveting.<br/><br/>The story initially jumps between the actual shooting in May and then following September when, Valerie is preparing to head back to school. Then it focuses on Valerie's senior year and the after math of the shooting itself. It's also laced with newspaper articles throughout the first half or so. These aspects really added a certain dynamic to the novel, and made it one that particularly stands out in my mind.<br/><br/>The narrative of this novel is so </span>
  <span id="freeText6773302836807723993" style="display:none">Three words: Powerful, thought-provoking, &amp; riveting.<br /><br />The story initially jumps between the actual shooting in May and then following September when, Valerie is preparing to head back to school. Then it focuses on Valerie's senior year and the after math of the shooting itself. It's also laced with newspaper articles throughout the first half or so. These aspects really added a certain dynamic to the novel, and made it one that particularly stands out in my mind.<br /><br />The narrative of this novel is so very compelling. It's definitely more of a character driven novel than plot driven, but for this particular situation it works really well. Valerie's guilt is depicted in a very realistic way, her struggle with her own identity, and her struggle to truly understand her feelings for Nick. It's just heartbreaking.<br /><br />This is definitely a topic that needs to be discussed and explored.<br /><br />A fantastically written, character driven novel, that you will not soon forget.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6773302836807723993" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_242463038" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/242463038" />
    <a title="Maria " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5769334-maria"><img alt="Maria " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1600318539p2/5769334.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/242463038?book_show_action=true">Dec 02, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maria " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maria " href="/user/show/5769334-maria">Maria </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer242463038" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2897829961883839261">This book reminded me of the song “Pumped-up Kicks” by Foster the People. It goes something like this: <br/><br/>All the other kids with the pumped up kicks,<br/> You better run, better run, outrun my gun.<br/> All the other kids with the pumped up kicks,<br/>You better run, better run, faster than my bullet.<br/><br/>In the song, the shooter’s name was Robert while the guy in this book was named Nick.<br/><br/>Nick was not a violent person.<br/>At first glance, you won’t even think of him as the guy who could do something like this.<br/>He was a ho</span>
  <span id="freeText2897829961883839261" style="display:none">This book reminded me of the song “Pumped-up Kicks” by Foster the People. It goes something like this: <br /><br />All the other kids with the pumped up kicks,<br /> You better run, better run, outrun my gun.<br /> All the other kids with the pumped up kicks,<br />You better run, better run, faster than my bullet.<br /><br />In the song, the shooter’s name was Robert while the guy in this book was named Nick.<br /><br />Nick was not a violent person.<br />At first glance, you won’t even think of him as the guy who could do something like this.<br />He was a hopeless romantic.<br /><br />But what pushed Nick to kill those students?<br /><br />BULLYING!<br /><br />I never experienced bullying when I was in high school so I couldn’t really related to how Nick and Valerie felt.<br />I felt for them though.<br />I hate it when other people think they’re better than anyone else.<br /><br />Nick and Valerie were one of the bullied ones.<br />Valerie showed Nick her hate list and it became some sort of their favorite pastime, bully-bashing behind their back.<br />Then one day, Nick came to school with a gun and killed the people on the list along with others unsuspecting students.<br />Val felt guilty because she felt that she had a hand on it somewhere even when she didn’t really give him the idea of that massive shooting.<br />She stopped him but still people talked.<br />They all think she had something to do with it, including her parent (which sucks!).<br /><br />The Hate List was one of those books that would open your eyes to the reality of life.<br />Like the other books I’ve read (Forbidden and But I love him), this book was something I would not forget anytime soon.<br />It was emotional and very real.<br />The book actually started after the incidents with little snippets of news about what happened during the shooting.<br />I was just a little disappointed that the characters lack back stories.<br />Although, I liked the concept, I didn’t really like how it was executed.<br />It was as if there was no other characters there than Valerie.<br />Everything focused on her.<br />I wanted to know more about Nick and what really pushed him to the edge.<br />Lack of character depth was acceptable but what I didn’t find acceptable was Valerie’s parents.<br />They were completely unfair.<br />They should have understood what she was going through not the other way.<br />They suck at parenting.<br />They let down their own daughter.<br />They should have believed her because she is their daughter.<br />Her own parent doesn’t even believe her and I think that must have been hard for Val.<br />I felt sympathy for Val and Nick.<br />They were victims here too just like the people Nick killed.<br />I am not saying that what Nick did was correct but what those bullies did to him was not correct either.<br />It wasn’t really clear what really caused Nick’s decision of really killing them because it was never really mentioned.<br />Not much about Nick was showed her which upset me a bit.<br />I wanted to know more about him.<br /><br />Anyways, it was a good attempt.<br />It was very light despite the sensitivity of the topic.<br />It was depressing yes but what can I say, it happens.<br />Bullying happens.<br />There are a lot of unloving parents out there too.<br /><br />I think the main lesson of this book is to respect one another.<br />We have to respect other people even if they are inferior to you.<br />There was this line from Harry Potter and the Goblet of Fire that I love so much and I think it would fit the moral lesson of the story.<br /><br />“If you want to know what a man's like, take a good look at how he treats his inferiors, not his equals.” <br /><br /><br />Need I say more?!<br /><br />I give this book 3.5 stars! :D<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2897829961883839261" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_623296888" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/623296888" />
    <a title="Olivia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3143889-olivia"><img alt="Olivia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1483879863p2/3143889.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/623296888?book_show_action=true">May 24, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Olivia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Olivia" href="/user/show/3143889-olivia">Olivia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780316041454" href="/book/show/7893725-hate-list">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer623296888" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5261815520883517487">I genuinely believe this is a life changing book - it's definitely made me think differently about life. Wow. Just, wow.<br/><br/>*FULL REVIEW BELOW.*<br/><br/>You know when you hear someone say, 'One day, you will find a book that will change the way you think about life.' Yeah? Well for me, that book was Hate List.<br/><br/>This book is one which hasn't got the most action packed plot, yet is rather driven by the stunning, multi-layered characters. Valerie, our main protagonist was such an interesting character to read abo</span>
  <span id="freeText5261815520883517487" style="display:none">I genuinely believe this is a life changing book - it's definitely made me think differently about life. Wow. Just, wow.<br /><br />*FULL REVIEW BELOW.*<br /><br />You know when you hear someone say, 'One day, you will find a book that will change the way you think about life.' Yeah? Well for me, that book was Hate List.<br /><br />This book is one which hasn't got the most action packed plot, yet is rather driven by the stunning, multi-layered characters. Valerie, our main protagonist was such an interesting character to read about, observing how she deals with the loss of her boyfriend, and her conflicting feelings as to whether it is right to love a 'monster.' Though Valerie's boyfriend, Nick - he shooter is dead, the book also carries his haunting voice throughout the book, which honestly gave me chills as I began to understand that he too, is a victim, a stupid, vulnerable victim.<br /> <br />The structure of this book is also what made it so strong. The book follows a chronological order, from the day of the shooting right up until a year after, yet manages to cleverly refer back to the accident through newspaper clipping, documenting the deaths and destruction that the shooting caused, constantly reminding the reader the effects of the tragedy and heightening the sheer emotion that this book possesses. <br /><br />This book honestly had such an emotional impact on me. Heck, I think I cried eight times! I feel so lucky that I got to read such a hauntingly beautiful book, and I believe that Valeries story of bravery and forgiveness, will stay with me for a long time. <br /><br />A million stars out of 5. </span>
  <a data-text-id="5261815520883517487" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer682133210704277929"><blockquote>
  <i>People do it all the time– assume that they know what's going on in someone else's head. That impossible. And to think it's possible is a really big mistake. A life-ruining one if you're not careful.</i>
</blockquote><br/><i>The Hate List</i> is about <b>perception</b> - how we can look at someone and see them as all bad or all good when they have tons beneath. Valerie perceived her boyfriend, Nick, as good – before he shot up their school. And everyone sees Valerie as bad, except for Jessica, the girl whose life Valerie saved.</span>
  <span id="freeText682133210704277929" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>People do it all the time– assume that they know what's going on in someone else's head. That impossible. And to think it's possible is a really big mistake. A life-ruining one if you're not careful.</i>
</blockquote><br /><i>The Hate List</i> is about <b>perception</b> - how we can look at someone and see them as all bad or all good when they have tons beneath. Valerie perceived her boyfriend, Nick, as good – before he shot up their school. And everyone sees Valerie as bad, except for Jessica, the girl whose life Valerie saved. <br /><br /><b>This didn't feel like a transparent attempt at starting Important Conversations On School Shootings.</b> In fact, as the author says herself, this book isn't about school shootings and trending topics. <br /><blockquote><i>I'll bet if you asked ten readers what Hate List was about, they'd say a school shooting. But for me, Hate List was never about a school shooting. This was always Valerie's story.</i> -Jennifer Brown</blockquote><br />True to the author's intent, <b>Valerie's story is truly what makes this book stand out</b>. She feels guilty for her role in what happened, however small, but she's not perfect. She still hates some of these people and she misses the one guy who made her feel happy, even though he was a monster. <b>Her character arc is one of the most solid I've read in contemporary fiction.</b><br /><br />I also want to give this book a shoutout for a great representation of ptsd and an <b>actually helpful counselor,</b> which - at the point I read this book - I literally think I had never seen in a book before. As someone who sees a therapist, and has an excellent relationship with said therapist (especially now, with a new one) I think it's important to show audiences that therapy, with the right person, is actually a deeply positive thing. <br /><br />Jessica and Valerie's relationship is maybe my favorite part of this entire book. The focus on <b>platonic friendship</b> as a way of healing rather than a romantic relationship really improved this book. So many books feel the need to insert a guy who can "teach the girl to love again", and in this case, I loved that <b>Val just needed a friend.</b><br /><br />VERDICT: <i>The Hate List</i> is an amazing, character-driven exploration of overcoming trauma that avoids the normal narratives of ~recovery boys~ in favor of friendship and primary agency to women. Definitely recommended.<br /><br /><a href="https://thebookishactress.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/thebookishactress" rel="nofollow noopener">Goodreads</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/jespergayhey" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/thebookishactress/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://sptfy.com/4E3o" rel="nofollow noopener">Spotify</a> | <a href="http://www.youtube.com/c/thebookishactress" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="682133210704277929" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1624237256" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1624237256" />
    <a title="Fabian {Councillor}" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/40792319-fabian-councillor"><img alt="Fabian {Councillor}" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1599133151p2/40792319.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1624237256?book_show_action=true">Apr 29, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Fabian {Councillor}" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Fabian {Councillor}" href="/user/show/40792319-fabian-councillor">Fabian {Councillor}</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Fabian {Councillor} by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/23304719-anne">Anne </a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40792319-fabian-councillor?shelf=read-2016">read-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40792319-fabian-councillor?shelf=ebook">ebook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40792319-fabian-councillor?shelf=onleihe">onleihe</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40792319-fabian-councillor?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40792319-fabian-councillor?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40792319-fabian-councillor?shelf=year-2009">year-2009</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1624237256" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17662539256908289711">If you are a student, then it is highly likely that you know about the constant fear of someone running on a killing spree in your school building or your university. If not, then at least you probably have relatives or friends who could potentially be involved in such a tragedy, just as everyone can possibly become a victim to such a horrifying scenario. That's what this book is about: the way an entire school deals with a killing spree after Nick Levil opened fire in the school cafeteria, kill</span>
  <span id="freeText17662539256908289711" style="display:none">If you are a student, then it is highly likely that you know about the constant fear of someone running on a killing spree in your school building or your university. If not, then at least you probably have relatives or friends who could potentially be involved in such a tragedy, just as everyone can possibly become a victim to such a horrifying scenario. That's what this book is about: the way an entire school deals with a killing spree after Nick Levil opened fire in the school cafeteria, killing several students and himself. I am not that well-informed about the circumstances in different countries, but here in Germany, tragedies like these have accompanied people for years, especially after the well-known and widely dreaded shooting sprees of Erfurt (2002), Emsdetten (2006) and Winnenden (2009). Emergency plans are now hanging on the doors of each classroom and instructions are given how to behave in such a case at the beginning of every schoolyear.<br /><br />But past events and the severe lack of security measures tell another story: that it would be easy for almost everyone to walk into a classroom or a lecture hall and kill at least ten people by random before someone can stop the killer. This is something which can never be truly predicted or prevented, not even with huge prevention activites (which, of course, cannot be found here at the moment). And this fear or becoming victim to such a tragedy as well as the aftermaths of it are what <i>Hate List</i> by Jennifer Brown deals with.<br /><br />Killing sprees are a serious topic which now and then invades the headlines and causes serious upheaval among the population. What makes it such a fascinating topic for an author to explore? It's the way they can't be predicted. Which thoughts have to run through the mind of a young person before walking through his or her school and killing dozens of people? How can such a deed be motivated? Why is it that nobody, not the parents, nor the friends, nor the girlfriend, ever sensed that something could happen?<br /><br />In this book, Valerie Leftman, the first-person narrator, is introduced as the girlfriend of the boy who killed those innocent people. While in their relationship, Nick was sweet, loving and caring, even though Valerie knew that he had some contacts to the wrong friends. In addition to that, Nick and Valerie, both considering themselves to be outsiders in their school, created a <i>Hate List</i> with the names of people they hate. And when Nick begins the shooting, those persons whose names appear on that list are chosen by him explicitly to be killed before finally he can be stopped, leading him to kill himself. When the book begins, five months have passed, and Valerie has to return to her school again. Everyone considers her to be the girlfriend of that killer, some even accuse her of having known about his plans, and nothing is going to make it easy for Valerie at her school.<br /><br />The social issue weighed heavily into this book, but apart from that, Valerie felt like a typical seventeen-year-old teenager to me, portrayed with almost the same character traits as all the other seventeen-year-old female protagonists in all those Young Adult novels out there. Her character had nothing special surrounding her, except for the constant self-pitying and selfishness. Her father was portrayed in a way which could not have been more negative, a way which is sadly too often occuring in reality. Her mother was portrayed in a way mothers shouldn't be portrayed, and the only character who sticked out to me as being interesting was Nick Levil, the perpetrator, for the mere fact that nobody suspected anything before he went on his killing spree. The most enthralling part of this novel was the way the author dealt with Nick's complicated mind; after all, what could turn a guy who reads Shakespeare for fun and has a (relatively) healthy social life into a killer?<br /><br />In the end, the premise convinced me most in this novel, while the characters fell flat for me and the plot balanced on a constant middle course between <i>boring</i> and <i>interesting</i>. However, it is possible that this novel was just a case of "it's me, not you", so I will recommend reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1352893030?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Anne's fantastic review</a> and let yourself be convinced that this book deserves to be checked out.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17662539256908289711" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1587042872" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1587042872" />
    <a title="Laurie –Read Between The Skylines–" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30004027-laurie-read-between-the-skylines"><img alt="Laurie –Read Between The Skylines–" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1466111136p2/30004027.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1587042872?book_show_action=true">Nov 10, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laurie –Read Between The Skylines–" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laurie –Read Between The Skylines–" href="/user/show/30004027-laurie-read-between-the-skylines">Laurie –Read Between The Skylines–</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Laurie –Read Between The Skylines– by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/23304719-anne">Anne </a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30004027-laurie-read-between-the-skylines?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30004027-laurie-read-between-the-skylines?shelf=standalone">standalone</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30004027-laurie-read-between-the-skylines?shelf=read-in-2016">read-in-2016</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1587042872" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9443722756768258209"><b>4.5 stars</b><br/><br/>It's been five months. Five months since that tragic day. That day when <b>Nick decides to open fire on his school cafeteria</b> killing those who were on the <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6316171.Hate_List' title='Hate List by Jennifer Brown' rel='nofollow noopener'>Hate List</a>. That list, which was written by him and his girlfriend Valerie, classified all those that used to torment them both during the school day. Students, bullies, teachers, popular kids... several of them were shot by Nick until Valerie tries to stop the slaughter, inadvertently saves a classmate and ends up being shot in the leg i</span>
  <span id="freeText9443722756768258209" style="display:none"><b>4.5 stars</b><br><br>It's been five months. Five months since that tragic day. That day when <b>Nick decides to open fire on his school cafeteria</b> killing those who were on the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6316171.Hate_List" title="Hate List by Jennifer Brown" rel="nofollow noopener">Hate List</a>. That list, which was written by him and his girlfriend Valerie, classified all those that used to torment them both during the school day. Students, bullies, teachers, popular kids... several of them were shot by Nick until Valerie tries to stop the slaughter, inadvertently saves a classmate and ends up being shot in the leg in the process. <br><br>After spending months in the hospital, where she is treated like a potential suspect and being sent to a psychological unit, she is finally sent home to rest and heal. It's now time to return to school to complete her senior year, <b>Valerie realizes that her worst wounds are not physical.</b> She will need to face hate, judgment and guilt. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1459844504ra/18659777.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I really loved how this book was written. I enjoyed both the writing style and the way both the past and the present were alternating. It's a subject that really touches me and I loved how it was handled. It wasn't only about victims and culprits. The Hate List was so layered and so deep, I recommend it to any reader.<br><br><u>Mild spoilers beyond this point</u>:<br><br>This book circles about perceptions. How to Valerie, the Hate List was a way to release herself as to Nick it was a list of potential targets. How they were both angry but that in the end, they didn't have the same perception of boundaries. Their perception of limits and retribution weren't on the same scale. And it was what amazed me the most. I think it was also what despaired Valerie the most and what made her <b>
  <u>denial</u>
</b> so hard to overcome. How two persons that close, always talking, sending texts and email to each other all night long, could be such strangers to one another? How could Valerie hadn't seen nor guessed what was happening in Nick's mind?<br><br>She was so lost that she ended up <b>
  <u>isolating</u>
</b> herself. She pushed away anyone that came to her, to help her. She rejected her family, her former friends and even classmates. I think that the fact that Nick killed himself made things worse for Valerie. She blamed herself for not seeing it coming. She was <b>
  <u>angry</u>
</b> at everyone including herself. It wasn't really about self-pitying, but more about the fact that she learned that the person she loved the most was a complete stranger and she couldn't ask for an explanation. She needed something, anything from him; a justification, an apology, or even a proof that she couldn't have known. Her whole world collapsed and she lost faith and trust toward her friends and family. <br><blockquote>
  <i>“Just like there's always time for pain, there's always time for healing.”</i>
</blockquote><br>It takes a long time to Valerie to stop <b>
  <u>bargaining</u>
</b> about what she could have done to prevent the tragedy. To have known better, and to have had some more insight into the slippery slope Nick was caught in. She has an amazing therapist, who is basically the only person she trusts, he helps her dealing with her feelings, her guilt and her <b><u>depression</u>,</b> to go through the day. To my opinion, when she started to go back to school, it was the beginning of the "going better process". Even though it was really hard for her to be confronted with the school situation, I think she was less dwelling on her misery. However, I understand how difficult it must have been for her to be stared and the object of murmurs and resentment. <br><br>The process of <b>
  <u>acceptance</u>
</b> is gradual and well brought. The main being about seeking forgiveness. Our closes ones' as well as our own. The more I read, <b>the more I realized that the most important was not the absolution of those she wronged, but her own acceptance</b> and mercy for herself. To accept that everyone deals with death and loss his or her own way and that it's okay to be mad, <b>it's okay to still love</b>, it's okay to stretch your hand to yesterday's foe and make him your friend. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1479671563ra/21221414.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="9443722756768258209" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1352893030" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1352893030" />
    <a title="Anne " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23304719-anne"><img alt="Anne " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1564193777p2/23304719.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1352893030?book_show_action=true">Aug 02, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anne " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anne " href="/user/show/23304719-anne">Anne </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1352893030" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12462955733417364701"> A WISE MAN ONCE SAID.<br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380424390ra/846029.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>Oh, don't roll your eyes. He <i>IS</i> wise!<br/><br/>▶<b>
  <i>
    <u> OVERVIEW </u>
  </i>
</b><br/><i>
  <blockquote>People hate. That's our reality. People hate and are hated and carry grudges and want punishments ... I don't know if it's possible to take hate away from people. Not even people like us, who've seen firsthand what hate can do. We're all hurting. We're all going to be hurting for a long time. And we, probably more than anyone else out there, will be searching for a new reality every day. A better one ... But in </blockquote></i></span>
  <span id="freeText12462955733417364701" style="display:none"> A WISE MAN ONCE SAID.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380424390ra/846029.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Oh, don't roll your eyes. He <i>IS</i> wise!<br><br>▶<b>
  <i>
    <u> OVERVIEW </u>
  </i>
</b><br><i>
  <blockquote>People hate. That's our reality. People hate and are hated and carry grudges and want punishments ... I don't know if it's possible to take hate away from people. Not even people like us, who've seen firsthand what hate can do. We're all hurting. We're all going to be hurting for a long time. And we, probably more than anyone else out there, will be searching for a new reality every day. A better one ... But in order to change reality you have to be willing to listen and to learn. And to hear. To actually hear.</blockquote>
</i><br><b>Five months ago, </b>Valerie Leftman was implicated in a tragic event that occurred in her high school's cafeteria. Now she has to return to those same halls and people who blame her for the crime which was committed, because Valerie's hate list was what prompted the high school shooting that marked a great change in the lives of the people of her hometown.<br> <b>Hate List</b> is very nearly an excellent piece of work that dares to be honest, sensitive and consequential in it's themes. <br>The story is told in present chapters, news reports and articles, flashbacks which take us through Valerie's memories of the day of the shooting, and the days before.<br><br>▶ <b>
  <i>
    <u>I'LL TELL YOU EXACTLY HOW I FELT WHILE AND AFTER READING THIS. </u>
  </i>
</b><br>I think this book changed me a bit. Sometimes when I read a story, no matter how invested I am, no matter how integrated I am into it, I imagine the story world is a glass globe, and I'm standing on the outside looking in. They say onlookers see much more than the players. I'm the onlooker, I should have aspired to more insight. But I didn't. I simply couldn't. And I swear I felt bamboozled and was very frustrated, like I was cheated out of my advantage and rightful privilege. I won't lie<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1425508813ra/13900161.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>BUT</b><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1457347136ra/18347693.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br> I've thought about the realities of this story and I still can't for the life of me understand the science behind them all. But I like this, this state of confutation is magnificent. It shouldn't be easy to assign blame, close the case and call it a day. It's wrong if it's that easy. It's wrong and inadequate. Many times I was angry at how thorough Brown was in exploring and communicating the feelings of the characters because I had no excuse to be lazy in my perceptions. <br><br>▶ <b>
  <i>
    <u>THIS WAS MY VERY FIRST BOOK ON THE SUBJECT OF HIGHSCHOOL SHOOTING.</u>
  </i>
</b><br><b>So like the heading says,</b> this was my very first book on the subject of highschool shooting, and I don't know if that should mean something. But it does, it really does, because in reality I had never thought about the subject and I never imagined I'd read a book on it. But we're readers and we keep circling in and out of orbit, so that's that. One thing that struck me about this story was the mundaneness of it's progression, the casualty of it's fuel source. Think about it. Have you ever made a list - and if not a physical list, a mental one - of things you hated, situations you wished you could take by the neck and wring the life out of, people you wanted gone, hurt, or both? Have you ever been that angry? Have you ever been that acidified? Burning and boiling and raging. And what if someone took that list and turned it into a gross reality. What if they turned your anger into something monstrously real and happening? Well, the answer is simple really.<br><br>Valerie started the <b>Hate List</b> that morphed into a target list which her boyfriend, Nick Levil, used to orchestrate an high school shooting. A shooting that left some dead, others hurt - including Valerie who was shot in the leg when she tried to stop the shooting, and Nick with a bullet in his head. Just thinking about this scene alone is dizzying. But the hardest part of the ordeal is the<b> blame assigning. </b> And along with that, the troubles of the aftermath: Dealing with loss and coming back to life after so many deaths, gaining back trust, forgiveness, friends, family and the love of a community that needs to grieve, and demands the comfort of having someone to blame. Those were the hardest parts, going through all those transitions were hard, not just for Valerie, but also for the reader. Because here is the time to doubt your sense of discernment. You're human, you'd love to blame someone too. We follow Valerie's shifts between different personas. Sometimes she's the sad girl and sometimes she's the monster. Sometimes she knows she tried her best and sometimes she's a failure. A hero. A victim. A culprit. An accomplice. It's all she could do to assume all these roles, to bear the burden of the crime she didn't commit, but somehow unconsciously permitted. <br><br> And then think about this, the greatest struggle after coming to terms with the deaths: That the boy you loved, a boy you felt one with at some point in your estranged lives could dip his hands into such dirty and dark things, use his hands to commit such an atrocity. How do you reconcile the love you feel with the crime? How do you reconcile your guilt with your role in the crime? Because even though Valerie wasn't aware of Nick's shooting plans, she did a bit more than just start the list, she helped it flourish by making namely contributions. She spewed hate and vented angrily. But she thought she was doing just that - venting. She didn't know Nick was <i>meaning</i> it. Meaning to take it one step further. Meaning for them to be the winners, just once.<br><blockquote>
  <i>“We all got to be winners sometimes. But what he didn’t understand was that we all had to be losers, too. Because you can’t have one without the other"</i>
</blockquote><br>One thing that frustrated the sanity out of me was <b>Nick.</b> Some characters in this book would have you believe that Nick was<u> a genetic waste.</u> Right from the womb, he was meant for trouble.<i> Yes, something wasn't quite right with that boy from the start. </i> But I wonder, is anyone ever born to be a high school shooter? Do some parents just wake up one morning and decide to have a baby that will be named catastrophe and carnage? A baby that will grow so full and tipping with hate and fury that he'd one day take a gun out and kill his school mates and himself? And if this isn't so, when did the poison set in? If he didn't come out bouncy with hate, then what? It all comes down to the time in between, it comes down to society. Society, environment and people. All the systems that mould us, change us, and break us. But you assume you know his mind. You conclude that because he killed, killing was his singular thought. You assume you know because it's easier that way. There's a reason, so logic has prevailed and all is right with the world again. But is it possible to know anyone's mind? To know without doubt all the emotions they're capable of feeling and things they're capable of doing?<br><blockquote>
  <i>"People do it all the time--assume that they "know" what's going on in someone else's head. That's impossible. And to think it's possible is a mistake. A really big mistake. A life-ruining one if you're not careful.”</i>
</blockquote><br>Don't you wonder about it? How shattered could a person be for them to lose that little bit of humanity that shuns murder and values something as fragile and invaluable as life? It's funny how people never asked the question <b>'why?'</b> And society in reality is exactly this way. I'm not saying the shooting is right, I'm not trying to downplay the tragedy but there's a cause to the effect. No one really took account of the fact that Nick and Valerie were harassed, abused and bullied day after day, because those are crimes less than murder. Just not bloody and stigmatizing enough to call for jail sentences and get the orange jumpsuits out. But we forget there is no grade to wrongness. I forgot this in the beginning, and every time Valerie tried to convince me of Nick's goodness, convince herself of his humanity, I forgot this - It's wrong because it's wrong. The bullying was wrong, and so was the shooting.<br><br>▶ <b>
  <i>
    <u>THE THEMES AND MOTIFS IN THIS BOOK WHICH I DARE. NOT EXPATIATE ON OR ELSE NOVEL.</u>
  </i>
</b><br>⏩ Versions of Reality.<br>⏩ Judgement - Valerie and Nick were so frivolous in their judgments. They hardly knew the truth of some people they placed on their list. <br>⏩ Tragedy.<br>⏩ Family and parental involvement.<br>⏩ Forgiveness.<br>⏩ Media.<br>⏩ Societal estrangements and constraints<br>⏩ The world of High school<br>⏩ Therapy and counseling. No seriously, if you meet the psychiatrist in this book you'll understand what I'm saying. Grateful is the word.<br>❎ Some people will probably abuse me for this, but I don't blame Valerie's parents for some of their reactions. I believe that it's not easy to be adequate in our reactions sometimes in the face of life changing tragic situations. But we try. We try and we fail. And that's the point of all these characters. But yes, a great big part of me kept wishing that someone would set Valerie's awful father straight... Or crooked.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1460257490ra/18719093.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>JK guys. JK.<br>▶ <b>
  <i>
    <u>WHAT IT MEANS TO FIND LOVE - UNHEALTHY LOVE - IN A HOPELESS PLACE.</u>
  </i>
</b><br>Something I found really harrowing was how unhealthy Nick and Valerie's relationship was. Sometimes it seemed like it needed hate to thrive. They needed to hate and be angry and spiteful to feel together. To be one in love. Nick and Valerie were odd kids, both alienated by the nature of their individual make-ups and circumstances that were out of their control - Broken families, troubled lives, insensitive peers. And lost knows lost, so they found themselves in each other and became lost together. I don't know honestly. I'm really, truly still doubting my deductions even after weeks following my reading. I'm doubting so much, this is just my two cents I'm putting in. Amidst all that hate, Valerie related moments of innocent love and untainted happiness that did nothing for my confusion. So I've come to the conclusion that their love was very schizophrenic. And yet they found comfort in it. Maybe it was all wrong and sully, but who and what could have saved them both? You understand through Valerie and Nick's relationship that in such a relationship, you could be happy. You could be really happy, but the question is for how long before you crash? <br>And so I say to you, define Masterpiece.<br><br>▶ <b>
  <i>
    <u>SONGS</u>
  </i>
</b><br>⏩ <b>Because my feelings will never be resolute, "Don't give a damn about your reasons" Nick.</b><br><a href="https://m.youtube.com/watch?v=3EL20VKlvbs" rel="nofollow noopener">Broken by James Bugg</a><br><br>⏩ <b>For Valerie</b><br><a href="https://m.youtube.com/watch?v=W0I6ZtWdM-Q" rel="nofollow noopener">Scars by Foxes</a><br><br>⏩ <b>For Graduation day! Time capsule scene :'( </b><br><a href="https://m.youtube.com/watch?v=KSIXU3XusSA" rel="nofollow noopener">Quiet In My Town by Civil Twilight</a><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1460286477ra/18722072.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>I NEED MEDICINE PEOPLE. </b><br><br><b>
  <u>PRE-REVIEW</u>
</b><br><b>I'D HONESTLY REALLY LOVE TO DO THIS:<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1442796019ra/16279306.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>But first I need to find the words.<br><br>Review to come when I'm less...<br><br>Words. Give. Me. Words.</b></span>

<div id="review_696272454" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/696272454" />
    <a title="C.G. Drews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews"><img alt="C.G. Drews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521552918p2/11375137.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/696272454?book_show_action=true">Aug 16, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="C.G. Drews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="C.G. Drews" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews">C.G. Drews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer696272454" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15264657010402511834">You know the kind of book that consumes you? I’m talking turns-you-into-a-hermit-until-you-read-the-last-page. HATE LIST is that kind of book. Emotional rollercoaster? Yes. <br/><br/>I wanted to cry. Scratch that – I wanted to bawl my eyes out. The book is about a school shooting, but then again, it isn’t about a school shooting. This is what the author’s note says (in the back of the book):<br/><br/><i> “Funny thing, I’ll bet if you asked ten readers what HATE LIST is about, they’d answer, ‘It’s about a school shooti</i></span>
  <span id="freeText15264657010402511834" style="display:none">You know the kind of book that consumes you? I’m talking turns-you-into-a-hermit-until-you-read-the-last-page. HATE LIST is that kind of book. Emotional rollercoaster? Yes. <br /><br />I wanted to cry. Scratch that – I wanted to bawl my eyes out. The book is about a school shooting, but then again, it isn’t about a school shooting. This is what the author’s note says (in the back of the book):<br /><br /><i> “Funny thing, I’ll bet if you asked ten readers what HATE LIST is about, they’d answer, ‘It’s about a school shooting.’ But for me, HATE LIST was never a story about a school shooting. From day one, this was always Valerie’s story.” </i><br /><br />That hit home for me. It’s so easy to take a book at face value. <i> Yup, the blurb says it’s about a school shooting. </i> NO. It’s about broken people and hating and recovering and selfishness. I want to bawl my eyes out, thinking about all this – because this book is about life. Just life. Screwed and messed up lives, but isn’t everyone in some way?<br /><br />It’s messy and gritty and horrible, but it’s not graphic. I’d say it’s aimed at a higher YA crowd, but besides the shooting elements, it’s actually about very normal kids. Alcohol and drugs are referenced, but not a big thing, you know? It’s about people. I think that’s why I loved it so much, because it wasn’t about a plot, it was about people.<br /><br />Valerie is the narrator. She’s 16, in high school, and her boyfriend, Nick Levill, was the shooter. But Valerie made “the list”. She and Nick were the underdogs. Trod on. Bullied. And they hated it. So they made a list, the Hate List, and wrote down just about everything they hated. And then one day Nick snapped and shot the people on the “list”. You know, the story is about spiraling out of control as well. The list didn’t start out as Valerie wanting to kill someone. She never wanted that. She began the list though, and said (off-handedly) she wanted to “kill” when a bully broke her MP3 player. She didn’t mean it. It was just a phrase. But it made me think, all the times we use phrases and talk about death without thinking about it. Wow.<br /><br />The character dynamics were really well written. Honestly, the characters just blew the socks off me. From the good side, to the people I wanted to scream at. I did. I mean, the book is about hate and everything, but gee, some of the characters made me loathe (see? I used loathe) them to the umpth degree. Wow and ouch. Her dad was just a dive. Her mum made me cry. Her brother? Even at the end, I wanted to shake Frankie and say, “Get a grip, dude. You have no idea.” <br /><br />I was so in the story, it felt like I was standing next to Valerie. I don’t know how she did it. I would have laid down and died. <br /><br />My only negativity is to the writing. It was a bit thick. I had to wade through pages of prose and description, when I think it could have been narrowed down. Less is more. The author tended to ramble.<br /><br />I’m giving this book 5-stars because it hit me hard. It dealt with life, on so many levels. I’m probably just going to be here eating chocolate and crying if you need me. Yup. My soul is shredded.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15264657010402511834" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
