  <span id="freeText17212726037310422191" style="display:none">3.5 stars. <br /><br />I thought the narrator did a really excellent job and the story was written in unique way (told from the MC’s point-of-view and through newspaper articles), but somewhere along the last third, I started to lose interest. I appreciated Valerie’s character and it was interesting to see her search for some sort of redemption despite the incident not being her fault. Her father really aggravated me, though, since he flat out said he would never forgive her and blames her for what happened. The climax and plot seemed to plateau around 55% and it never really recovered. I did enjoy the story and feel it’s an important one, but I wasn’t blown away.</span>

<div id="review_1367782253" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1367782253" />
    <a title="Em Lost In Books" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11166121-em-lost-in-books"><img alt="Em Lost In Books" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1522743986p2/11166121.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1367782253?book_show_action=true">Sep 21, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Em Lost In Books" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Em Lost In Books" href="/user/show/11166121-em-lost-in-books">Em Lost In Books</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11166121-em-lost-in-books?shelf=stand-alone-read">stand-alone-read</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1367782253" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10425096192515286929">This book had so much potential because of its subject but it failed miserably at every level. <br/><br/>Val with her boyfriend Nick made a hate list, writing names of people who bullied them and whom they hated. One fine day, Nick started shooting his school mates who were on hate list, and after killing many of them he shot himself. <br/><br/>This book is told from Val's PoV, relaying her life before and after the shooting. Though author made school shooting the main subject of this book but I think she is not ab</span>
  <span id="freeText10425096192515286929" style="display:none">This book had so much potential because of its subject but it failed miserably at every level. <br /><br />Val with her boyfriend Nick made a hate list, writing names of people who bullied them and whom they hated. One fine day, Nick started shooting his school mates who were on hate list, and after killing many of them he shot himself. <br /><br />This book is told from Val's PoV, relaying her life before and after the shooting. Though author made school shooting the main subject of this book but I think she is not able to explain the reason behind it. Is bullying the main reason behind this? Or is it how Val and Nick's parents neglected them? Both of these points were presented as the excuses that pushed Nick towards shooting other students. Author never went deeper and told what Val and Nicm went through. She remained on surface and Val and Nick were just two whining kids running away from bullying instead of talking about if with elders.<br /><br />The other thing that bugged me most was behavior of Val's parents. They were so angry with her and blamed her fir ruining their lives. I think Brown made up them like that to make reader believe that to a large extent they're the reason that Val felt so isolated and made that hate list.<br /><br />Also I hated Val. She kept crying all the time, running away from her life at school. Always making excuses for Nick, that he was a good guy. Come on girl, no matter how good the boy was but he still killed his classmates. He put deceaseds' parents through hell and many other kids who survived thd bullets but didn't want to live anymore because of mental trauma.<br /><br />The only good thing about the book was how it ended. It was a sad book and author didn't do a great job of telling us about what these kids went through after the shooting and the reason behind the shooting. Am not recommending this to anyone.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10425096192515286929" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('y+GPyi4zQQ2lwHp/PHn9GlaawQRoH6n19AWDf/d/4T8sOYFuUeOnXumxIP/ezwDrOlzX+LWEBTtHHid/1honmQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('fvLT80ERhH/9ofr6zNbva2FReZ55WMtaupFNLTN4EDqZKt1XPsFiLLHQoHouYBKaDZdvYqTDZ5QJiuktEh3WnA==')})
  }
//]]>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer6854436713681725529">Two-time winner of the Erma Bombeck Global Humor Award (2005 & 2006), Jennifer's weekly humor column appeared in The Kansas City Star for over four years, until she gave it up to be a full-time young adult novelist. <br/><br/>Jennifer's debut novel, HATE LIST (Little, Brown Books for Young Readers, 2009) received three starred reviews and was selected as an ALA Best Book for Young Adults, a VOYA "Perfect Te</span>
  <span id="freeText6854436713681725529" style="display:none">Two-time winner of the Erma Bombeck Global Humor Award (2005 &amp; 2006), Jennifer's weekly humor column appeared in The Kansas City Star for over four years, until she gave it up to be a full-time young adult novelist. <br /><br />Jennifer's debut novel, HATE LIST (Little, Brown Books for Young Readers, 2009) received three starred reviews and was selected as an ALA Best Book for Young Adults, a VOYA "Perfect Ten," and a School Library Journal Best Book of the Year. HATE LIST also won the Michigan Library Association's Thumbs Up! Award, the Louisiana Teen Readers Choice award, the 2012 Oklahoma Sequoyah Book Award, was an honorable mention for the 2011 Arkansas Teen Book Award, is a YALSA 2012 Popular Paperback, received spots on the Texas Library Association's Taysha's high school reading list as well as the Missouri Library Association's Missouri Gateway Awards list, and has been chosen to represent the state of Missouri in the 2012 National Book Festival in Washington, DC. Jennifer's second novel, BITTER END, (Little, Brown Books for Young Readers, 2011) received starred reviews from Publishers Weekly and VOYA and is listed on the YALSA 2012 Best Fiction for Young Adults list and is a 2012 Taysha's high school reading list pick as well.<br /><br />Jennifer writes and lives in the Kansas City, Missouri area, with her husband and three children.</span>
